Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
10 min
Majority Consensus with Rare Opposition: Is It Binding?
Defines ijma' al-akthar and analyzes its status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ijma' al-akthar and apply the distinction between qat'i and zanni proof.

Core Idea
Majority consensus is not true ijma'; 'all' is the basis for infallibility.

This passage examines a nuanced usul issue: when the majority of mujtahids agree but one or two dissent, does that agreement carry binding authority? The Hanafi school distinguishes between full ijma' (of all) and majority agreement, treating the latter as a conjectural proof at best. Understanding this distinction helps you evaluate the strength of different types of scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage asks: Is the consensus of the majority (ijma' al-akthar) considered ijma' when there are rare dissenters (one or two)? The author presents two positions: some say it is ijma', others say it is not.
Focus on the chosen view: it is not ijma'.
2
Examine the Hanafi position
The chosen view is that ijma' al-akthar is not true ijma' because 'all' (al-kull) is absent, and 'all' is the basis for infallibility (ismah). Then scholars differ on whether it is any proof at all: some say no, some say it is a zanni (conjectural) proof.
Note the epistemological weight: zanni versus qat'i.
3
Analyze the evidence and counterarguments
The passage presents opposing evidence: a hadith that 'the hand of Allah is with the group' and the example of Abu Bakr's caliphate where initial opposition was resolved. The Hanafi response interprets the hadith as referring to full consensus, not merely majority, and notes that in Abu Bakr's case, eventual consensus was achieved.
See how the author reframes the dalil.
4
Apply the distinction to examples
The passage gives several historical examples: the Companions' agreement on 'awl (except Ibn Abbas), on nullification of wudu by sleep (except Abu Musa), and on fasting while traveling (except Abu Huraira and Ibn Umar). In each case, the dissenters were rare but the majority consensus did not become ijma'.
These illustrate the practical implication.
5
Synthesize the ruling and its impact
The thamarah al-khilaf: for a mujtahid, the majority view is not obligatory to follow; he may adopt the minority view if his ijtihad leads to it. A judge cannot enforce it as binding ijma'.
This shows the practical importance of the classification.

الأكبر اتفقوا على عدم جواز قتال مانعي الزكاة وهو رضي الله تعالى عنه خالفهم فقط، بل الذي ثبت رضي الله عنه لما هم بقتال مانعي الزكاة اشتبه ذلك على أمير المؤمنين عمر بقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله فكشف شبهته بأنه رجع داخل في الاستثناء فوافقه وأجمع عليه الصحابة كافة وقاتلوا معه فليس هذا من الباب في شيء فاحفظه (والمختار أنه ليس بإجماع لانتفاء (الكل) الذي هو مناط العصمة، ثم اختلفوا (فقيل ليس بحجة أصلاً) كما أنه ليس بإجماع (وقيل: بل حجة ظنية) غير الإجماع (لأن الظاهر إصابة السواد الأعظم) إذ من البعيد أن لا يطلع الأكثر بعد الفحص الشديد ويطلع الواحد الأندر (قيل ربما كان الحق الأقل) وليس فيه بعد ألا ترى الفرقة الناجية واحدة من ثلاث وسبعين) وقد ارتد أكثر الناس بعد وفاته عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام والمؤمنون أقل من الكفرة وكان الأكثر من الناس في زمان بني أمية على إمامة معاوية مع أن الحق كان بيد أمير المؤمنين علي كرم الله وجهه من غير ريبة (و) على إمامة (يزيد) ابنه مع أنه كان من أخبث الفساق وكان بعيداً بمراحل من الإمامة بل الشك في إيمانه خذله الله تعالى، والصنيعات التي صنعها معروفة من أنواع الخبائث (وأشباههما) من الظلمة والفسقة، والحاصل : أن الحق ربما كان الأقل ولا بعد فيه والمذكورات إسناد (أقول : كثرة الفرق لا مع تستلزم كثرة الأشخاص) بل يجوز أن تكون أشخاص الفرقة الواحدة أكثر من أشخاص سائر الفرق فوحدة الفرقة الناجية لا توجب كون الحق مع الأقل وكثرة الأشخاص لا تستلزم كثرة العدول والمجتهدين) وقائلو إمامة معاوية لم يكونوا مجتهدين اللهم إلا نادراً وقائلوا إمامة يزيد وأشباهه لم يكونوا عدولاً بل من أغلظ الفسقة ( والنزاع) إنما وقع (فيه) فإن الظاهر من اتفاق أكثر المجتهدين العدول الإصابة (فتأمل) فيه فإنه لا يزيد على الكلام على السند. قال في «الحاشية» المقصود دعوى ظهور الإصابة ولما كان الاشتباه لهذا الإسناد تكلم عليه، وأنت لا يخفى عليك أن دعوى الظهور لا تخلو عن كدر فتأمل المكتفون بإجماع الأكثر (قالوا أولاً) قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (يد الله مع الجماعة فمن شذ شذ في النار) رواه أصحاب السنن ومثله في صحيح البخاري قلنا محمول على الإجماع) أي على إجماع الكل بناء على أنه يمنع المخالفة بعد الموافقة لأنه أي شذ من شذ البعير) إذا تواحش بعدما كان أهلياً (و) قالوا (ثانياً : صح خلافة أمير المؤمنين وإمام الصديقين (أبي بكر رضي الله عنه صحة لا يرتاب فيها إلا من سفه نفسه مع خلاف) أمير المؤمنين (علي) كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام وسعد بن عبادة وسلمان الفارسي ولو كان الشرط إجماع الكل لما الإجماع على الخلافة الواضح الصحة مثل وضوح الشمس، ثم عد سلمان غير صحيح فإنه لم ينقل عنه التوقف أصلاً، كيف وسلمان من تلامذة إمام الصديقين وأصحاب الإمام العارف خواجه بهاء الدين نقشبند قدس سره من الأولياء يروون أخذه التصوف منه رضي الله عنه، وينسبون خرقة إرادته إليه رضي الله تعالى عنه ويدفع بأن الإجماع بعد رجوعهم إلى بيعته ( رضي الله عنه هذا واضح في أمير المؤمنين علي فإنه قد روى عبد الرزاق عن معمر عن لأبي بكر تخلف علي عن بيعته وجلس في بيته فلقيه عمر فقال : تخلّفت بويع لابي قال عكرمة قال لما صح هذا عن بيعة أبي بكر؟ فقال إني آليت بيمين حين قبض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم أن لا أرتدي برداء إلا إلى الصلاة المكتوبة حتى أجمع القرآن فإني خشيت أن ينفلت، ثم خرج فبايعه كذا في الاستيعاب». ثم اختلفت الروايات في زمان التوقف ففي صحيح ابن حبان أنه بايع بعد ثلاثة أيام وصححه القسطلاني وفي الصحيحين بعد ستة أشهر وقال بعض أهل التحقيق أنه كرّم الله وجهه بايع بيعتين أولهما : بعد ثلاثة أيام بقبول الخلافة، وثانيهما: بعد ستة أشهر، لما وقع المشاجرة في فدك وغيره ولما زعم الناس التباغض ولم يكن لهم ذلك الزعم كيف وأمثال أمير المؤمنين على براء منه وللتفصيل موضع آخر لكن رجوع سعد بن عبادة
Issue: It is said that the consensus of the majority with the rarity of the dissenter, whether one or two, is consensus, like others besides Ibn Abbas agreed on the saying of al-‘awl when the shares exceed the estate. This is according to the well-known view, otherwise it will come that the denial of al-‘awl is not authentically reported from him. And others besides Abu Musa al-Ash‘ari agreed on the nullification of ablution by sleep, and others besides Abu Huraira and Ibn ‘Umar agreed on the permissibility of fasting while traveling. In it is an indication that Abu Huraira was a jurist, as is correct, and it has passed. And it is said: if the majority permitted his ijtihad while he opposed them, like the opposition of the Commander of the Faithful, the Imam of the Truthful, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq regarding those who refrained from paying the alms, where he uniquely ruled to fight them, then consensus is not formed with his opposition, unlike the statement of Ibn Abbas on the permissibility of surplus in ribawi goods, for they did not permit his ijtihad, rather they rebuked him repeatedly until he retracted what he said, as in Sahih Muslim, and it is narrated from him: O Allah, I repent from my saying on currency and my saying on temporary marriage. And in the first example there is consideration, for it is not proven that others besides the Commander of the Faithful, the Great Truthful, agreed on the impermissibility of fighting the Zakat preventers, and he (may Allah be pleased with him) only opposed them. Rather, what is proven is that when he (may Allah be pleased with him) intended to fight the Zakat preventers, this was ambiguous to the Commander of the Faithful ‘Umar due to his statement: I was commanded to fight people until they say there is no god but Allah. So he removed his ambiguity by saying that they are included in the exception, so he agreed, and all the Companions agreed and fought with him. So this is not of the subject at all, so preserve it. And the chosen view is that it is not consensus due to the absence of 'all' which is the basis for infallibility. Then they differed: it is said it is not a proof at all, just as it is not consensus; and it is said it is a conjectural proof besides consensus, because the apparent is the correctness of the great majority, since it is unlikely that the majority after thorough examination do not discover the truth while the rare one does. It is said: perhaps the truth is with the minority, and there is no improbability in it; do you not see that the saved sect is one out of seventy-three? And most people apostatized after his death, and the believers were fewer than the disbelievers. And most people in the time of the Umayyads were upon the imamate of Mu‘awiya, while the truth was with the Commander of the Faithful ‘Ali without doubt. And upon the imamate of Yazid his son, even though he was among the worst of the transgressors, and was far from imamate, rather doubt in his faith. Allah forsake him. And the deeds he did are well-known from types of wickedness. And their likes among the oppressors and transgressors. The conclusion: perhaps the truth is with the minority, and there is no improbability in it. The mentioned ones are asnad. I say: the multitude of sects does not necessarily entail the multitude of individuals. Rather, it is possible that the individuals of one sect are more than the individuals of all other sects. So the unity of the saved sect does not necessitate that the truth is with the minority. And the multitude of individuals does not necessitate the multitude of just and mujtahids. And those who held the imamate of Mu‘awiya were not mujtahids, except rarely, and those who held the imamate of Yazid and his likes were not just, but rather from the worst transgressors. And the dispute is only about that, for the apparent from the agreement of most just mujtahids is correctness. So ponder over it, for it does not exceed speech about the chain. He said in al-Hashiya: The purpose is the claim of apparent correctness, and since the ambiguity is for this chain, he discussed it. And it is not hidden from you that the claim of being apparent is not free from turbidity, so ponder. Those satisfied with the consensus of the majority said: First, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The hand of Allah is with the group, so whoever deviates, deviates to the Fire. Reported by the authors of the Sunan, and similar is in Sahih al-Bukhari. We say it is carried upon consensus, i.e., upon the consensus of all, based on that it prevents opposition after agreement, because 'shadhdha' means to go astray like a camel that becomes wild after being tame. And secondly, they said: The caliphate of the Commander of the Faithful, the Imam of the Truthful, Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) was established with a clarity that none doubts except one who debases himself, despite the opposition of the Commander of the Faithful ‘Ali and the faces of his noble family, and Sa‘d ibn ‘Ubada, and Salman al-Farsi. And if the condition were consensus of all, there would be no consensus on the caliphate which is as clear as the sun. Then the count of Salman is not correct, for no hesitation was reported from him. How can it be, while Salman was among the students of the Imam of the Truthful and the followers of the Imam al-‘Arif Khwaja Baha’ al-Din Naqshband? The saints relate his taking of Sufism from him, and they attribute the cloak of his will to him. And it is repelled by the consensus after their return to his pledge. This is clear concerning the Commander of the Faithful ‘Ali, for ‘Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Ma‘mar from ‘Ikrima: ‘Ali lagged behind from his pledge and sat in his house. ‘Umar met him and said: You have lagged behind when the pledge has been given to Abu Bakr? He said: I swore an oath when the Messenger of Allah died that I would not put on a cloak except for the obligatory prayer until I compile the Quran, for I feared it would be lost. Then he came out and pledged to him. Thus in al-Isti‘ab. Then the narrations differed regarding the time of hesitation. In Sahih Ibn Hibban, he pledged after three days, and al-Qastallani authenticated it. In the two Sahihs, after six months. Some investigators said that he gave two pledges: the first after three days accepting the caliphate, and the second after six months, due to the dispute over Fadak and other matters. And the people alleged hatred, but they did not have that claim. How can it be? The likes of the Commander of the Faithful are innocent of it. For detail there is another place. But the return of Sa‘d ibn ‘Ubada...
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the rule of majority consensus (ijma' al-akthar) when there are rare dissenters. The author presents the view that such consensus is considered ijma' by some, citing examples: the Companions (except Ibn Abbas) agreed on the principle of 'awl in inheritance, except that his denial is not proven; except Abu Musa on the nullification of wudu by sleep; except Abu Huraira and Ibn 'Umar on fasting while traveling. Then he contrasts the case of the majority permitting the dissenter's ijtihad (like Abu Bakr's unique ruling to fight zakat refusers) versus cases where they did not permit it (like Ibn Abbas on riba, where he retracted). He then analyzes the example of Abu Bakr and shows that ultimately all Companions agreed, so it is not a real exception. The chosen view is that majority consensus is not true ijma' because 'all' is missing, which is the basis for infallibility. Then scholars differ on whether it is a proof at all: some say no, some say it is a zanni proof because the majority is likely correct. The author presents counterarguments that truth may be with the minority, citing examples: the saved sect is one, many apostatized after the Prophet, the majority supported Mu'awiya and Yazid, but truth was with Ali. He then refutes these examples by noting that the majority in those cases were not just or mujtahids. The discussion includes hadith evidence ('the hand of Allah is with the group') interpreted as referring to consensus of all, not just majority. The caliphate of Abu Bakr is presented as an example where opposition by Ali and others was resolved through later return to consensus. The passage ends with a discussion of the timeline of Ali's pledge.

Key Terms
إجماع الأكثر (ijmā‘ al-akthar): Agreement of the majority of mujtahids in an age, with one or two dissenting
السواد الأعظم (al-sawād al-a‘ẓam): The great majority, the multitude
حجة ظنية (ḥujja ẓanniyya): A conjectural proof, not certain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi chosen view in this passage, what is the status of consensus of the majority (ijma' al-akthar) with a rare dissenter?
A) It is a binding ijma' (qat'i proof)
B) It is not ijma' and not a proof at all
C) It is not ijma' but may be considered a zanni proof
D) It is ijma' only if the dissenter retracts

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that majority consensus lacks the essential condition of 'all' for infallibility, so it is not binding ijma', though it may serve as a conjectural proof.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced
10 min
The Condition of Extinction of the Era in Silent Consensus
Debating whether extinction of the era is a condition for silent consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the condition of extinction of the era in silent consensus, identify the opposing argument, and apply the Hanafi response using textual and logical proofs.

Core Idea
Silent consensus is binding from the moment of agreement; extinction of the era is not required.

This passage delves into a key usul dispute: does silent consensus require the extinction of the era (the death of all mujtahids of that generation) to become binding? The Hanafi school argues it does not, and the text presents a detailed refutation of the condition, citing textual evidence and logical arguments. Understanding this debate is crucial for grasping the authority of consensus in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly what the Hanafi school holds regarding the condition of extinction of the era: it is not required; consensus is binding upon its occurrence.
The text says: 'لنا الدليل على العصمة اتفاق الكل من الأمة بالنص وقد وجد ولو لمحة فوجب عصمته.'
2
Understand the opposing view
Some scholars, including Imam al-Haramayn, condition extinction, at least when the basis is qiyas. Understand the rationale: analogy to the Prophet's era where consensus was not binding due to his presence.
The opposing argument is based on the idea that as long as mujtahids survive, reversal is possible.
3
Follow the Hanafi refutation of infinite regress
If extinction were required, consensus would never occur due to successive mujtahids. The text answers by noting that such succession is not necessary and that consensus did occur in early generations.
Key phrase: 'لو شرط انقراض العصر لما وجد إجماع لتلاحق المجتهدين.'
4
Analyze the story of Ali and Abu Ubayda
The incident illustrates that once consensus appears (even between two caliphs), retraction is not accepted, supporting the Hanafi position that extinction is not needed.
Even though the author notes some obscurities, the story is used as a proof against the condition.
5
Assess the final argument on the statement of the dead
Opponents say that if a dissenter dies, his statement is no longer considered, so the living become the whole ummah. The Hanafi response: the dead mujtahid's proof lives on, so his opinion remains part of the consensus.
The text distinguishes between the person being dead and his proof being alive.

Source Text

مع وجود الأصل الثالث الإجماع (وقيل) : شرط (في) الإجماع (السكوتي) فقط (و) قال (الإمام) إمام الحرمين : (إن كان سنده قياساً) فشرط وإلا لا ، كذا) في المختصر والصحيح أن الشرط عنده حينئذ) أي حين كان السند قياساً (تطاول (الزمان) لا انقراض العصر (فلو هلكوا بغتة بعد الاتفاق لا إجماع عنده) الانقراض لفقد التطاول (لنا الدليل على العصمة (اتفاق الكل من الأمة بالنص (وقد وجد ولو لمحة فوجب عصمته، وبهذا القدر تم الدليل لكن زيد عليه لزيادة التوضيح والاستئناس لعدم الاشتراط (و) قيل ذلك لأن الانقراض لا مدخل له في الإصابة ضرورة فتأمل وما في «الحاشية» إشارة إلى أن حجية الإجماع ليست عقلية بل أمر ،تعبدي ألا ترى أنه لم يكن حجة في زمانه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام فكما كان انقراض زمانه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم شرطاً فكذا يجوز أن يكون انقراض عصر المجتهدين أيضاً شرطاً فلا يزيد على الكلام على التوضيح ولا يضر أصل الاستدلال، وأما في حياته صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فلا تحقق للإجماع لكفاية قوله، وبلغو الاجماع لا أن الاجماع لو وقع لم يكن حجة فالقياس عليه فارق واستدل لو (شرط) انقراض العصر (لما وجد إجماع لتلاحق المجتهدين) مع أي لحوقهم مرة بعد أخرى فلو توقف الاجماع على الانقراض ووجد مجتهد وجب دخوله، ثم يجب انقراضه فيجب دخول آخر لاحق قبل انقراضه وهكذا وأجيب أولاً كما في شرح الشرح بأن التلاحق للمجتهدين ليس بواجب، بل غايته الجواز فمن أين يلزم عدم تحقق الإجماع) بل غاية ما يلزم جواز عدم تحقق الإجماع ولا فساد فيه قيل : إنه واجب عادة وإن لم يجب عقلاً) فإن العادة جرت بوجود مجتهد في كل عصر (أقول للمنع مجال) فإنّ جريان العادة في القرون السابقة مسلم وأما في كل عصر ففي حيز الخفاء (والأوجه) في دفع «شرح الشرح» أن يقال : ( إن المراد) لو شرط لزم عدم تحققه في زمان قد أجمعوا على تحققه فيه) أي في زمان تحققه فيه مسلم بيننا وبينكم وهو زمان الصحابة والتابعين وتابعيهم وحينئذ لا يمنع اللحوق) للمجتهدين، ولا لأنه معلوم الوقوع فتدبر و أجيب :(ثانياً : بأن الشرط إنما هو انقراض) المجمعين (الأولين) فقط لا انقراض اللاحقين ولو قيل بمدخلية اللاحقين في تحقق الإجماع، وحينئذ لا يلزم عدم تحقق الإجماع. وأما إذا قيل بعدم مدخلية اللاحقين بأن يكون الإجماع إجماع المجمعين لكن الحجية مشروطة بالانقراض فعدم اللزوم أظهر، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن الانقراض لو كان شرطاً لكان لاحتمال ظهور الحجة بخلافه والرجوع إليه وهذا متحقق في كل من له دخل في الإجماع فالمجتهد اللاحق إن كان الإجماع بدون رأيه غير معتبر فلا بد من انقراض عصره أيضاً لقيام الاحتمال المذكور وإن لم يكن له دخل في الإجماع، بل بدونه فهذا باطل لأنه إذا شرط الانقراض فقبله لا حجة أصلاً فجاز مخالفة اللاحق بالرأي ويكون قوله معتبر فوقت الحجية وهو وقت الانقراض لم يوجد قول كل الأمة فانتفى الإجماع وحينئذ اتجه الدليل واندفع الكلامان الأخيران فتأمل الشارطون (قالوا: أولاً يؤدي) عدم الاشتراط المذكور إلى منع المجتهد عن الرجوع) عن مذهبه (عند ظهور موجبه) أي موجب الرجوع (ولو) كان ذلك الموجب خبراً صحيحاً) واجب العمل واللازم باطل (قلنا منقوض بما بعد الانقراض فإنه يلزم منع المجتهد عن مخالفته مع وجود الموجب ولو كان خبراً صحيحاً، والحل منع بطلان التالي لأنا نلتزم المنع عن الرجوع ولا نسلم إمكان الموجب لأن الإجماع قاطع) فلا يصح دليل في مقابلته (قال) أبو عبيدة بفتح العين السلماني (لعلي) أمير المؤمنين (حين رجع عن عدم صحة بيع أم الولد) روى البيهقي عن أمير المؤمنين علي أنه خطب على منبر الكوفة فقال : اجتمع رأيي ورأي أمير المؤمنين عمر أن لا تباع أمهات الأولاد، وأما الآن فأرى بيعهن، فقال عبيدة السلماني رأيك مع الجماعة أحب إلي والمحفوظ إلينا (من رأيك وحدك فأطرق علي رضي الله عنه ثم قال اقضوا ما أنتم قاضون فأنا أكره أن أخالف أصحابي. وفي رواية عبد الرزاق رأيك ورأي عمر في الجماعة أحب إلي من رأيك وحدك في الفرقة، فضحك علي رضي الله عنه، كذا في فتح القدير. فقد ظهر من هذا أن الرجوع غير صحيح عند وقوع الإجماع مرة وإلا لما أنكر أبو عبيدة على أمير المؤمنين علي وتوقف هو عن الرجوع، كذا قالوا وفيه خفاء فإن هذا إنما يدل على اتفاق رأي أميري المؤمنين لا على اتفاق آراء الكل، وقول أبو عبيدة أيضاً لا يدل عليه لأن الجماعة تقع على ما فوق الاثنين، ولذا قال أحب إليّ ولم يقل رأيك وحدك خطأ قطعاً وأما رجوع أمير المؤمنين عن هذا القول فلعله لرجوع رأيه إلى ما كان كما هو الظاهر أو لم يرجع لكن أمرهم بالثبات على ما كانوا عليه کراهية أن ينتقلوا من رأي مجتهد التزموه على أنفسهم فافهم ثم إنه لو كان على عدم جواز البيع إجماع لزم كون قول أمير المؤمنين إما خارقاً للاجماع وشأنه أجل من ذلك، وإما لأن الانقراض شرط عنده وهو أيضاً بعيد منه، وأيضاً لم يتوجه إليه ما قال أبو عبيدة فافهم ولا يبعد أن يقال المقصود منه الاستناد والقدر الثابت فيه كاف لأنه لما أنكر الرجوع عن موافقة البعض أو الأكثر لكونهم في طبقة عليا فأي استبعاد في حرمة مخالفة الإجماع والرجوع بعد فتأمل (و) قالوا (ثانياً: لو لم يعتبر قول الراجع من المجمعين بعد الإجماع (لأن الأول اتفاق الأمة) لا يجوز خرقه الوجب عدم اعتبار قول من مات من (المخالفين في الإجماع اللاحق لأن الباقي كل الأمة فيكون اتفاقهم حجة (قلنا : قد يمنع بطلان اللازم ويلتزم عدم اعتبار قول من مات (لأن قول الميت كالميت فلا يعتبر (وقد يمنع الملازمة وعليه الأكثر لأن قوله) أي قول من مات (حي بدليله فهو كبقائه أي كبقاء الميت حين (الانعقاد للإجماع فلم يلزم الاتفاق وأما فيما نحن فقد وجد الاتفاق ولو لمحة (فتأمل) .
With the existence of the third source, consensus. (It was said): a condition (in) consensus (silent) only. And (Imam) Imam al-Haramayn said: (If its basis is qiyas) then it is a condition, otherwise not, like that in al-Mukhtasar. And the correct view is that the condition in his view then, i.e., when the basis is qiyas, is the prolongation of time, not the extinction of the era. (So if they died suddenly after agreement, there is no consensus in his view) due to loss of prolongation. (For us is the proof of infallibility) the agreement of all of the ummah by textual evidence, and it has occurred even for a moment, so its infallibility is binding. With this extent the proof is complete, but more was added for greater clarification and reassurance for not requiring the condition. (And) it was said that because extinction has no role in correctness necessarily, so reflect. And what is in al-Hashiyah indicates that the authority of consensus is not rational but a devotional matter. Do you not see that it was not a proof in his time (peace be upon him and his family and companions)? So just as the extinction of his time was a condition, similarly it is possible that the extinction of the era of the mujtahids is also a condition. So it does not increase beyond the discussion on al-Tawdih and does not harm the original proof. And during his life (peace be upon him and his family and companions) there is no realization of consensus due to the sufficiency of his statement, and the reaching of consensus does not mean that if consensus occurred it would not be a proof. So the analogy upon it differs. And he argued: If (the condition of) extinction of the era (were required, then consensus would never occur due to the successive arrival of mujtahids) with any of their arrivals one after another. So if consensus were dependent on extinction and a mujtahid appeared, his inclusion is necessary, then his extinction is necessary, then the inclusion of another later one before his extinction, and so on. And it was answered first, as in Sharh al-Sharh, that the successive arrival of mujtahids is not obligatory; rather its utmost is permissibility. So from where does the non-realization of consensus necessarily follow? Rather the utmost that follows is the possibility of non-realization, and there is no corruption in that. It was said: It is usual even if not intellectually obligatory, for custom has it that a mujtahid exists in every age. I say: There is room to deny this, for the prevalence of the custom in previous centuries is conceded, but in every age it is hidden. And the best (way) to refute Sharh al-Sharh is to say: (The meaning is) if it were a condition, it would necessarily not be realized in a time in which they have agreed upon its realization, i.e., the time of the Companions, the Successors, and their followers. And then the arrival of mujtahids does not prevent it, nor because its occurrence is known. So ponder. And it was answered secondly: (That the condition is only the extinction of the first consensus participants) alone, not the extinction of the later ones, even if one says there is inclusion of later ones in the realization of consensus. And then the non-realization of consensus does not follow. And if one says there is no inclusion of later ones, so that the consensus is the consensus of the participants but its validity is conditional upon extinction, then the non-necessity is even more apparent. And it should not be hidden from you that if extinction were a condition, it would be due to the possibility of the emergence of a proof contrary to it and reverting to it, and this possibility is realized in everyone who has a role in consensus. So the later mujtahid: if consensus without his opinion is not considered, then the extinction of his era is also necessary due to the mentioned possibility; and if he has no role in consensus, then it is invalid because if extinction is a condition, before it there is no proof at all, so it is permissible for the later one to oppose with his opinion, and his statement is considered. So the time of validity, which is the time of extinction, the statement of the whole ummah does not exist, so consensus is negated. And then the proof is directed, and the two last statements are repelled. So reflect. The stipulators (said: Firstly, it leads) the non-requirement mentioned to prevent the mujtahid from retracting from his madhhab when its cause appears, even if that cause is a sound hadith that is obligatory to act upon, and the consequent is false. (We say: It is rebutted by what happens after extinction, for it necessitates preventing the mujtahid from opposing it with the existence of the cause even if it is a sound hadith. And the solution is to reject the falsity of the consequent, for we commit to preventing retraction, and we do not concede the possibility of the cause because consensus is conclusive, so no proof can stand against it.) (He said) Abu Ubayda (with fatha on 'ayn) al-Sulmani (to Ali) the Commander of the Faithful: (when he retracted from the ruling of the invalidity of selling Umm al-Walad). Al-Bayhaqi narrated that Ali addressed on the minbar of Kufa: 'My opinion and the opinion of the Commander of the Faithful Umar agreed that the mothers of children should not be sold, but now I see their sale.' So Ubayda al-Sulmani said: 'Your opinion with the group is more beloved to me, and what is preserved with us, than your opinion alone.' So Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) lowered his head, then said: 'Judge what you will, for I dislike to oppose my companions.' And in a narration of Abd al-Razzaq: 'Your opinion and Umar's opinion in the group are more beloved to me than your opinion alone in division.' So Ali laughed. So it has appeared from this that retraction is not valid when consensus has occurred once, otherwise Abu Ubayda would not have objected to Ali and he would not have held back from retraction. Thus they said, but there is obscurity in it, for this only indicates the agreement of the two commanders, not the agreement of all. And the statement of Abu Ubayda does not indicate it either, because 'the group' applies to more than two, and therefore he said 'more beloved to me' and did not say 'your opinion alone is definitely wrong'. As for Ali's retraction from this statement, perhaps it was due to his opinion returning to what it was, as is apparent, or he did not retract but ordered them to remain on what they were doing, disliking that they should move from a mujtahid's opinion they had committed to. So understand. Then if there were consensus on the impermissibility of sale, then Ali's statement would either be a breach of consensus – and his stature is greater than that – or because extinction is a condition in his view – and that is also far from him. And also, what Abu Ubayda said was not directed at him. So understand. And it is not far to say that the purpose is reliance and the established capacity is sufficient, because when he objected to retraction from agreement with some or the majority due to their being in a high rank, what improbability is there in the prohibition of opposing consensus and retracting after? So reflect. (And) they said (secondly: If the statement of the retracting participant in consensus after consensus were not considered, because the first agreement of the ummah cannot be breached, then it would necessitate not considering the statement of those who died from (the dissenters in the later consensus) because the remaining are the whole ummah, so their agreement is a proof. (We say: The falsity of the consequent may be denied, and we commit to not considering the statement of the dead) because the statement of the dead is like the dead, so it is not considered. (And the correlation may be denied, and upon this are the majority, because his statement) i.e., the statement of the dead, (is alive through his proof, so it is like his continuation, i.e., like the continuation of the dead at the time of the formation of consensus, so agreement does not follow. And as for in our case, agreement has occurred even if just for a moment (so reflect).
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion on the condition of extinction of the era (انقراض العصر) for silent consensus (الإجماع السكوتي). The author presents several views: some say it is a condition only for silent consensus, others (like Imam al-Haramayn) condition it only when the basis is qiyas, and he substitutes prolongation of time for extinction. The Hanafi position is that extinction is not a condition; consensus is binding from the moment it occurs, based on the textual proof that agreement of the whole ummah is infallible (عصمة). The passage then refutes the condition by showing it leads to an infinite regress (تلاحق المجتهدين) preventing consensus from ever being established, which is false since consensus occurred in the era of the Sahaba. The story of Ali (RA) and Abu Ubayda is cited to show that once consensus is achieved, retraction is not valid, though the author notes obscurities in using this as proof. Finally, the argument that the statement of a dead mujtahid is not considered in later consensus is refuted by distinguishing between the statement being dead in person but alive through its proof. The author concludes that consensus has been achieved even for a moment, so extinction is unnecessary.

Key Terms
الإجماع السكوتي (al-ijmā‘ al-sukūtī): Consensus where some scholars remain silent after hearing the opinion of others, indicating tacit approval.
انقراض العصر (inqirāḍ al-‘aṣr): The extinction of the era, i.e., the death of all mujtahids of a particular generation.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is required for silent consensus to become binding?
A) The extinction of the era of the mujtahids
B) The prolongation of time
C) The occurrence of agreement, even for a moment
D) The presence of a sound hadith

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that silent consensus is binding upon its occurrence, without waiting for the extinction of the era, based on the definitive textual evidence of the infallibility of the ummah's agreement.

Consensus After Disagreement: The Mut'at al-Umrah Example
Arguing for the validity of consensus in a later generation after earlier disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the validity of consensus after earlier disagreement and apply it to the example of mut'at al-umrah.

Core Idea
A later consensus can be binding even after earlier disagreement; the actual occurrence proves its possibility.

If the Companions disagreed on a ruling, can the Successors later agree on one opinion and form a binding consensus? This is a foundational question in usul al-fiqh. This lesson examines the Hanafi view that such consensus is possible, using the historical example of the Successors' agreement on mut'at al-umrah (combining Umrah and Hajj).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the passage debates whether a consensus (ijma) that occurs after a known disagreement in the earlier generation is valid and binding.
This is a methodological question about the conditions of ijma.
2
State the opposing view
Note that Ash'ari, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, al-Ghazali, and Imam al-Haramayn hold such consensus is impossible because the earlier disagreement prevents any later claim of unanimity.
Their reasoning: the dissenting opinions of the first generation remain valid options; later agreement cannot erase them.
3
State the chosen view
The majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is hold that it is possible and binding (al-mukhtar: waqi‘ hujja).
This is the author's preferred view.
4
Examine the proof
The proof adduced is the consensus of the Successors on the permissibility of mut'at al-umrah, despite earlier Companion disagreement.
The actual occurrence of this consensus demonstrates that such consensus is possible in principle.
5
Understand the example
Mut'at al-umrah refers to combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey. The author clarifies that jurists use 'qiran' for one ihram and 'tamattu' for two ihrams.
The text is cut off, but the point is that the Successors agreed on its permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: اتفاق العصر الثاني بعد استقرار الخلاف في العصر (الأول ممتنع عند الأشعري و الإمام أحمد (و) الإمام حجة الإسلام الغزالي والإمام إمام الحرمين (والمختار أنه واقع حجة وعليه أكثر الحنفية والشافعية : لنا على الوقوع إجماع التابعين على جواز متعة العمرة) أي الجمع بينهما بإحرام واحد أو بإحرامين في أشهر الحج والفقهاء يطلقون القرآن على الأول، والمتعة على الثاني والمصنف جرى على الاطلاق القديم ( وقد كان أمير المؤمنين (عمر أو) ،
Issue: The agreement of the second generation after established disagreement in the first (generation is impossible according to Ash'ari and Imam Ahmad (and) Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali and Imam al-Haramayn (and the chosen view is that it is actual and a proof, and upon it is the majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is. For us on its occurrence: the consensus of the Successors on the permissibility of mut'at al-umrah) i.e., combining them with one ihram or two ihrams in the months of Hajj. The jurists apply 'qiran' to the first and 'tamattu' to the second, and the author followed the old terminology. (And the Commander of the Faithful (Umar or) ,
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage addresses a disputed issue: can there be a binding consensus in the second generation (e.g., the Successors) after the first generation (e.g., the Companions) had a known disagreement on a matter? Some scholars, like Ash'ari, Ahmad, Ghazali, and Imam al-Haramayn, hold that such consensus is impossible because the earlier disagreement prevents any later claim of unanimous agreement. However, the chosen position (al-mukhtar) is that it is possible and constitutes a proof (hujja). The majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is support this. The proof adduced is the consensus of the Successors on the permissibility of 'mut'at al-umrah' — a specific combination of Umrah and Hajj. The passage explains that 'qiran' and 'tamattu' are terms used by jurists; the author follows the old usage. The mention of 'Amir al-Mu'minin (Umar or)' is cut off, but it likely refers to a statement of Umar or Uthman regarding this practice. The incomplete text suggests the argument continues.

Key Terms
متعة العمرة (mut‘at al-‘umrah): Combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey, either with one ihram (qiran) or two ihrams (tamattu‘) during the Hajj months.
القرآن (al-qirān): The combination of Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram, intending both at once.
المختار (al-mukhtār): The chosen or preferred opinion among the scholars of the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following scholars held that consensus of the second generation after disagreement in the first is impossible?
A) Imam al-Shafi'i
B) Imam Abu Hanifa
C) Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal
D) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts later ijma as binding even after earlier ikhtilaf, as proven by the Successors' consensus on mut'at al-umrah.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

The Prohibition of Retraction After Ijma': The Case of 'Ali and Abu 'Ubayda
Analyzing the impossibility of a mujtahid retracting after consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument that a mujtahid cannot retract after ijma' is formed, using the story of 'Ali and Abu 'Ubayda as a naqli dalil.

Core Idea
Once consensus is established, no mujtahid may oppose it, even with a sound hadith.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi position that ijma' (consensus) is a decisive proof that cannot be overturned by a later ijtihad, even if the mujtahid discovers a stronger evidence. The central proof is the historical incident involving Imam 'Ali and the companion Abu 'Ubayda. By examining this incident, we understand how the Companions themselves treated collective agreement as binding, providing a foundation for the rule that retraction from a consensus is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The issue is whether a mujtahid can retract his opinion after the ummah has reached consensus on a ruling, especially if he later finds a sound hadith that seems to contradict the consensus.
The Hanafi school holds that retraction is invalid; others disagree.
2
State the Hanafi position and evidence
The Hanafi position is that ijma' is qat'i (decisive) and no proof can stand against it. The evidence is the story of 'Ali and Abu 'Ubayda, which shows that 'Ali did not insist on his new view after being reminded of the earlier agreement with 'Umar.
The proof is a qawl sahabi (statement of a Companion) transmitted by al-Bayhaqi and 'Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Analyze the story in detail
Read the narration: 'Ali initially agreed with 'Umar that slave mothers (umm walad) should not be sold. Later he opined that they could be sold. Abu 'Ubayda objected, saying his opinion with the group (i.e., with 'Umar) was more beloved. 'Ali bowed his head and said he hated to oppose his companions, effectively retracting.
Note that Abu 'Ubayda did not say the new opinion was wrong, but preferred the earlier collective view.
4
Examine objections to the proof
Objections raised: (1) This only shows agreement of two, not all mujtahids; (2) Abu 'Ubayda's statement is a preference, not a definitive ruling; (3) 'Ali may not have truly retracted but ordered them to stay with the earlier practice.
The author refutes these by arguing that even partial agreement with senior companions carries weight, and the principle of stability supports the prohibition of retraction.
5
Apply the principle to a scenario
Consider a situation where later scholars discover a hadith that contradicts a ruling established by consensus. According to the Hanafi view, that hadith cannot override the consensus because ijma' is decisive.
This highlights the practical consequence: fatwa based on consensus is stable and not overturned by later ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد الانقراض فإنه يلزم منع المجتهد عن مخالفته مع وجود الموجب ولو كان خبراً صحيحاً، والحل منع بطلان التالي لأنا نلتزم المنع عن الرجوع ولا نسلم إمكان الموجب لأن الإجماع قاطع) فلا يصح دليل في مقابلته (قال) أبو عبيدة بفتح العين السلماني (لعلي) أمير المؤمنين (حين رجع عن عدم صحة بيع أم الولد) روى البيهقي عن أمير المؤمنين علي أنه خطب على منبر الكوفة فقال : اجتمع رأيي ورأي أمير المؤمنين عمر أن لا تباع أمهات الأولاد، وأما الآن فأرى بيعهن، فقال عبيدة السلماني رأيك مع الجماعة أحب إلي والمحفوظ إلينا (من رأيك وحدك فأطرق علي رضي الله عنه ثم قال اقضوا ما أنتم قاضون فأنا أكره أن أخالف أصحابي. وفي رواية عبد الرزاق رأيك ورأي عمر في الجماعة أحب إلي من رأيك وحدك في الفرقة، فضحك علي رضي الله عنه، كذا في فتح القدير. فقد ظهر من هذا أن الرجوع غير صحيح عند وقوع الإجماع مرة وإلا لما أنكر أبو عبيدة على أمير المؤمنين علي وتوقف هو عن الرجوع، كذا قالوا وفيه خفاء فإن هذا إنما يدل على اتفاق رأي أميري المؤمنين لا على اتفاق آراء الكل، وقول أبو عبيدة أيضاً لا يدل عليه لأن الجماعة تقع على ما فوق الاثنين، ولذا قال أحب إليّ ولم يقل رأيك وحدك خطأ قطعاً وأما رجوع أمير المؤمنين عن هذا القول فلعله لرجوع رأيه إلى ما كان كما هو الظاهر أو لم يرجع لكن أمرهم بالثبات على ما كانوا عليه کراهية أن ينتقلوا من رأي مجتهد التزموه على أنفسهم فافهم ثم إنه لو كان على عدم جواز البيع إجماع لزم كون قول أمير المؤمنين إما خارقاً للاجماع وشأنه أجل من ذلك، وإما لأن الانقراض شرط عنده وهو أيضاً بعيد منه، وأيضاً لم يتوجه إليه ما قال أبو عبيدة فافهم ولا يبعد أن يقال المقصود منه الاستناد والقدر الثابت فيه كاف لأنه لما أنكر الرجوع عن موافقة البعض أو الأكثر لكونهم في طبقة عليا فأي استبعاد في حرمة مخالفة الإجماع والرجوع بعد فتأمل (و) قالوا (ثانياً: لو لم يعتبر قول الراجع من المجمعين بعد الإجماع (لأن الأول اتفاق الأمة) لا يجوز خرقه الوجب عدم اعتبار قول من مات من (المخالفين في الإجماع اللاحق لأن الباقي كل الأمة فيكون اتفاقهم حجة (قلنا : قد يمنع بطلان اللازم ويلتزم عدم اعتبار قول من مات (لأن قول الميت كالميت فلا يعتبر (وقد يمنع الملازمة وعليه الأكثر لأن قوله) أي قول من مات (حي بدليله فهو كبقائه أي كبقاء الميت حين (الانعقاد للإجماع فلم يلزم الاتفاق وأما فيما نحن فقد وجد الاتفاق ولو لمحة (فتأمل) . (1) الراوي المذكور في أسماء الرجال عبيدة بدون أبو ، قال في الخلاصة مات النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو في الطريق، قال وهو نظير شريح في العلم والقضاء. اهـ. وفي بعض النسخ قال : عبيدة على الصواب. اهـ. كتبه مصححه .
After extinction, it necessitates preventing the mujtahid from opposing it [ijma'] while the cause exists, even if it is a sound hadith. The solution is to deny the invalidity of the consequent, for we commit to preventing retraction and we do not concede the possibility of a [valid] cause because ijma' is decisive; so no proof is valid against it. Abu 'Ubayda (with fatha on 'ayn) al-Sulmani said to 'Ali, the Commander of the Faithful, when he retracted from the impermissibility of selling a slave mother of children (umm walad). Al-Bayhaqi narrated from 'Ali that he gave a sermon from the minbar of Kufa and said: 'My opinion and the opinion of 'Umar agreed that slave mothers should not be sold, but now I see their sale [as permissible].' 'Ubayda al-Sulmani said: 'Your opinion with the group is more beloved to us, and what is preserved with us, than your opinion alone.' So 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, bowed his head, then said: 'Decide as you will, for I hate to oppose my companions.' In the narration of 'Abd al-Razzaq: 'Your opinion and 'Umar's opinion in the group is more beloved to me than your opinion alone in separation.' So 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, laughed. This is in Fath al-Qadir. So it appears from this that retraction is not valid once consensus has occurred; otherwise, Abu 'Ubayda would not have objected to 'Ali and he would not have paused from retraction. Thus they said, but there is subtlety: for this only indicates agreement of the two Commanders of the Faithful, not agreement of all. The statement of Abu 'Ubayda also does not indicate that, because 'group' applies to more than two, and therefore he said 'more beloved to me' and did not say 'your opinion alone is definitely wrong'. As for 'Ali's retraction from this statement, perhaps because his opinion returned to what it was, as is apparent, or he did not retract but ordered them to remain as they were, disliking that they should shift from the opinion of a mujtahid which they had adopted for themselves. Understand this. Then, if there were consensus on the impermissibility of sale, then 'Ali's statement would either be a breach of consensus—and his status is too high for that—or because extinction is a condition for him, which is also far from him. Also, the statement of Abu 'Ubayda does not apply to him. Understand this. It is not far to say that the purpose was reliance, and the established import is sufficient, because when he objected to retracting from the agreement of some or most, due to them being in a high rank, then what improbability is there in the prohibition of opposing consensus and retracting after it? So reflect. And they said, secondly: If the statement of the retracting person from among the consensus-holders after consensus were not considered—because the first agreement of the ummah cannot be breached—then it would necessitate that the statement of those who died from the dissenters in the later consensus is not considered, because the remaining are the entire ummah, so their agreement is authoritative. We say: The invalidity of the consequent may be denied, and we accept that the statement of the dead is not considered because the statement of the dead is like a dead person, so it is not considered. And the entailment may be denied, and this is the view of the majority, because his statement (i.e., the statement of the one who died) is alive through its evidence, so it is like his continued existence, i.e., like the continued existence of the dead at the time of the formation of consensus; so agreement does not follow. As for our case, agreement has occurred, even if fleeting. So reflect. (1) The narrator mentioned in the books of narrators is 'Ubayda without 'Abu'; in al-Khulasa: 'He died while the Prophet, peace be upon him, was on the path; he is analogous to Shurayh in knowledge and judgment.' End. In some copies: 'He said: 'Ubayda is correct.' End. Written by its corrector.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the binding nature of ijma' and the possibility of a mujtahid retracting after consensus. The author argues that once consensus is formed, it is decisive and cannot be opposed even by a sound hadith. He supports this with the story of 'Ali and Abu 'Ubayda: when 'Ali changed his view on selling Umm Walad, Abu 'Ubayda objected, preferring 'Ali's earlier opinion with the group (i.e., with 'Umar) over his new solo opinion. 'Ali then acquiesced, showing he disliked opposing his companions. The author addresses objections: this only shows agreement of two, not all; Abu 'Ubayda's statement was preference, not certainty; 'Ali may not have truly retracted. The second argument concerns whether the opinion of a deceased mujtahid is still considered in later consensus. The author concludes that agreement did occur in this case, but the issue of retraction remains debated.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): The consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah after the death of the Prophet on a legal ruling.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Retraction or withdrawal by a mujtahid from his previous ijtihad or fatwa.
الانقراض (al-inqirad): The extinction of the entire generation of mujtahids who originally held differing opinions, as a condition for the binding nature of later consensus?

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam 'Ali not insist on his new view allowing the sale of Umm Walad after Abu 'Ubayda's objection?
A) Because he realized his new opinion was based on a weak hadith.
B) Because he disliked opposing his companions and the collective agreement.
C) Because Abu 'Ubayda threatened him with punishment.
D) Because he was uncertain about the ruling.

Key Takeaway
A mujtahid cannot retract his opinion after ijma' has been formed, even if he finds stronger evidence, because ijma' is a decisive proof.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced
8 min
The Status of a Deceased Mujtahid's Opinion in Later Consensus
Debate on whether a mujtahid's opinion survives his death for consensus purposes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Hanafi argument regarding whether the opinion of a deceased mujtahid is considered in the formation of later consensus, and identify the majority view.

Core Idea
The opinion of a mujtahid lives through its evidence; the dead mujtahid's statement retains authority even after death.

This lesson examines a second objection to the Hanafi position on retraction: if a mujtahid retracts before death, does his earlier opinion still count in consensus? More broadly, we explore whether the opinion of a deceased mujtahid continues to affect the formation of later consensus. The passage presents two opposing views and invites reflection. Understanding this nuance deepens our appreciation of how consensus is formed and maintained across generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second objection
The objection is: If the first mujtahid's retraction is not considered after consensus because the earlier consensus cannot be breached, then what about the opinions of mujtahids who died before the later consensus? Should their opinions be counted in the later consensus?
This is a logical extension of the principle that consensus is binding.
2
State the two responses
The author presents two responses: (1) The opinion of a dead mujtahid is not considered—his statement is like a dead person, so it is like he never existed. (2) The opinion is alive through its evidence, so it is as if the mujtahid is still present for the purpose of consensus.
Response (2) is attributed to the majority (الأكثر).
3
Analyze the majority view
The majority view holds that the evidence behind a mujtahid's opinion does not die with him. Therefore, his opinion remains a valid contribution that can affect the formation of later consensus, either as part of the consensus or as a dissenting view.
This view is more consistent with the principle that proofs are permanent.
4
Relate to the earlier principle
If the dead mujtahid's opinion is alive, then even after his death, his earlier opinion (if it was against the later consensus) prevents the formation of full consensus, making the later agreement not truly ijma'.
This reinforces the stability of earlier rulings.
5
Determine the author's inclination
The author ends with 'فتأمل' (so reflect), indicating that the issue is not definitively settled in this passage. However, the later tradition of the Hanafi school leans towards the majority view that the opinion lives through evidence.
In practice, Hanafi usul accepts that a deceased mujtahid's opinion retains authority.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced

Possibility and Bindingness of Later Consensus After Earlier Disagreement
Debating whether consensus can arise in a later century after earlier disagreement and its authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position on later ijma' from the opposing view, identify the two historical examples used as proof, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf for the ruling on selling Umm Walad.

Core Idea
Later consensus after earlier disagreement is binding and can settle disputed rulings.

This passage tackles a fundamental usul question: can the mujtahids of a later century reach a binding consensus on a matter that was disputed by earlier scholars? The author presents the debate and defends the majority view that such consensus is possible and authoritative. Through the examples of Mut'at al-Hajj and Umm Walad, we see how this principle impacts practical fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the view of al-Ash'ari et al. (impossible) and the majority (possible and authoritative).
The author declares the chosen position as al-mukhtar.
2
Examine the first proof: Consensus on Mut'at al-Hajj
Note that the Companions (Umar/Uthman vs Ali) had ikhtilaf, yet later Followers agreed on permissibility. The author defends this consensus against objections about the authenticity of the Companions' prohibition.
The prohibition by Uthman is countered by Ali's practice; Umar's prohibition is not reliably established.
3
Examine the second proof: Consensus on Umm Walad
Note earlier Companion disagreement and later consensus on prohibition. The author notes this consensus is not reliably established.
This consensus is disputed; the author casts doubt on its authenticity.
4
Analyze the counterarguments and response
The opposing view: earlier ikhtilaf means truth is with one, later consensus cannot override. Hanafi response: earlier opinion may die out; ummah cannot agree on error.
The author acknowledges the weakness of the Hanafi argument ('Fihi ma fihi').
5
Connect to thamarah al-khilaf
For Mut'at al-Hajj: later consensus confirms permissibility. For Umm Walad: if later consensus is binding, sale is invalid; if not, a judge's sale may be valid (Abu Hanifa's variant).
The intra-Hanafi difference on Umm Walad hinges on this usul dispute.

Source Text

لنا على الوقوع إجماع التابعين على جواز متعة العمرة) أي الجمع بينهما بإحرام واحد أو بإحرامين في أشهر الحج والفقهاء يطلقون القرآن على الأول، والمتعة على الثاني والمصنف جرى على الاطلاق القديم ( وقد كان أمير المؤمنين (عمر أو) أمير المؤمنين (عثمان ينهي عنه أما نهي أمير المؤمنين عثمان فثابت في «الصحيحين»، وغيره في الحاشية في صحيح البخاري أن مروان قال : شهدت عثمان وعلياً وعثمان ينهي عن المتعة وأن يجمع بينهما، فلما رأى علي أهل بهما : لبيك بعمرة وحجة وقال : ما كنت لأدع سنة النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لقول أحد ، ثم الروايات متظافرة، فلا يضر كون الراوي مروان، وأما نهي أمير المؤمنين عمر فلم يثبت بسند صحيح، لكن يروى في غير المعتبرات أن كان يقول : ثلاث كن على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه عمر وسلم أنا أحرمهن وأنهي عنهن متعة الحج ومتعة النكاح وحي على خير العمل فإن صح فمعناه أن الثلاثة التي وقعت في العهد الشريف أحياناً أنا أبين حرمتهن التي تبنت منه عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام وأنهي عنهن لأجل الحرمة الثابتة في الشرع الشريف بعد الإباحة وأراد بمتعة الحج فسخ الحج بالعمرة، ثم الحج بالإحرام في يوم قبل عرفة فإنه وإن وقع في حجة أحد الوداع لكنه كان مختصاً بالصحابة كما قال أبو ذر رواه مسلم وهذا موافق لما عنه في روي الصحيحين أنه قال لعلي أن الله يقول: ﴿ وَأَتِمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلهِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٩٦] جميعاً وأما رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فقد ساق الهدي فلم يحل. وأما متعة النساء وإن أبيحت يوم خيبر لكن حرمت بعد ذلك إلى يوم القيامة وحي على خير العمل قد نسخ في العهد الشريف، ولهذا تواتر الآذان ،بدونه، وإنما وصف الثلاثة بكونهن في العهد الشريف رداً لمن يتوهم الجواز بسماع أنها كانت فأزال الوهم بأنها وإن كانت لكن لم تبق عليكم فافهم، وإنما آثرنا نوعاً من الأطناب لأن بعض السفهاء من الروافض يطفئون نور الله بأفواههم ويقولون : إن أمير المؤمنين حرم ما كان مباحاً في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وهو كبيرة فلا يلتفت إليه (و) لنا إجماع التابعين على عدم جواز بيع أم الولد وقد اختلفت الصحابة فيه إجماع التابعين على جواز متعة الحج لعله واضح فإنهم كانوا معلومين عرف منهم عمل التمتع والفتوى به في أيام الحج لاجتماعهم فيها وأما إجماعهم على حرمة بيع أم الولد فلم يصح بعد ولم ينقل بوجه يقبله العقل وقوانين الصحة (وأما الحجية) أي حجية هذا الإجماع (فلئلا يلزم خلو الزمان عن الحق واتفاق الأمة على الخطأ المنفي عنهم بالنص (وفيه ما فيه) لأن خلو الزمان عن الحق ممنوع وإنما يلزم لو لم يكن قول المجتهد الأول باقياً، وهو في حيز الخفاء، فإنّ بقاءه ببقاء الدليل لا ببقاء القائل وهو موجود، وإن قيل قد مات بهذا الاتفاق قلنا هذا فرع حجية الاتفاق وفيه الكلام بعد فافهم. ثم إن الإمام أبا حنيفة ذهب في رواية إلى نفاذ بيع أم الولد بحكم القاضي خلافاً لهما فقيل : هذا مبني على أن الخلاف السابق يمنع الإجماع اللاحق وإلا فقد انعقد إجماع التابعين على عدم الجواز والقضاء مخالف الإجماع لا ينفذ، فأراد المصنف دفع هذا القول وقال (وما) روي عن أبي حنيفة في غير الظاهر) من الرواية (من نفاذ القضاء أم الولد خلافاً لهما على ما في «الميزان»، وذكر شمس الأئمة أن أبا يوسف ببيع مع أبي حنيفة فلأن المسألة مسألة حجية هذا الإجماع (اجتهادية) فعند من يرى هذا الإجماع حجة لم ينفذ القضاء وعند من يرى عدم الحجية ينفذ فنفاذه مختلف فيه فينفذ إذا وجد إمضاء
Issue: Agreement of the second century after settlement of disagreement in the first century is impossible according to al-Ash'ari, Imam Ahmad, Imam al-Ghazali, and Imam al-Haramayn. The chosen position is that it occurs and is authoritative, and this is the view of most Hanafis and Shafi'is. Our evidence for its occurrence is the consensus of the Followers (Tabi'un) on the permissibility of Mut'at al-'Umrah, i.e., combining them with one ihram or two ihrams during the months of Hajj. Jurists apply 'Qiran' to the first and 'Tamattu' to the second; the author follows the old usage. The Commander of the Faithful 'Umar or 'Uthman used to forbid it. As for the prohibition by 'Uthman, it is firmly established in the two Sahihs and others. In the margin of Sahih al-Bukhari: Marwan said: 'I witnessed 'Uthman and 'Ali, and 'Uthman was forbidding Tamattu' and combining them. When 'Ali saw him, he said: 'Labbayk bi 'Umrah wa Hajj' and said: 'I would not leave the Sunnah of the Prophet for the saying of anyone.' Then the narrations are numerous, so the fact that the narrator is Marwan does not harm. As for the prohibition by 'Umar, it is not established with a sound chain, but it is narrated in unreliable sources that he used to say: 'Three things were [permitted] in the time of the Messenger of Allah, and I forbid them and prohibit: Tamattu' of Hajj, Tamattu' of marriage, and 'Hayya 'ala khayr al-'amal'. If this is authentic, its meaning is that I explain their prohibition which is derived from him, peace be upon him, and I prohibit them due to the established prohibition in the noble Shari'ah after permission. By Tamattu' of Hajj, he meant annulling Hajj for 'Umrah, or Hajj with ihram on the day before 'Arafah; though this occurred in the Farewell Hajj, it was specific to the Companions as Abu Dharr said, narrated by Muslim. This agrees with what is in the two Sahihs that he said to 'Ali: 'Allah says: 'Complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' [2:196] altogether; and the Prophet brought the sacrificial animal, so he did not become free.' As for Tamattu' of women, though permitted on the day of Khaybar, it was thereafter prohibited until the Day of Judgment. And 'Hayya 'ala khayr al-'amal' was abrogated in the noble era, hence the call to prayer is established without it. The description of the three as being in the noble era is a refutation of those who mistakenly think permission remains upon hearing they existed; so he removes the illusion that they existed but not for you. Understand this. We have chosen a type of elaboration because some foolish Rawafid try to extinguish the light of Allah with their mouths and say that the Commander of the Faithful prohibited what was permitted in the time of the Prophet and his Companions, which is a major sin. So pay no attention. Also, we have the consensus of the Followers on the impermissibility of selling Umm Walad, despite the Companions' disagreement on it; and the consensus of the Followers on the permissibility of Mut'at al-Hajj is clear, for they were known, and the practice of Tamattu' and fatwa on it were well-known during the days of Hajj due to their gathering. As for their consensus on the prohibition of selling Umm Walad, it has not been established after, nor has it been transmitted in a way acceptable to reason and the laws of authenticity. As for the authority of this consensus, it is to avoid the time being devoid of truth and the ummah agreeing on error, which is negated from them by text. But this has its own issues, because the time being devoid of truth is denied; rather it would follow only if the statement of the first mujtahid were not remaining, which is obscure. Its remaining is by the remaining of the evidence, not by the remaining of the speaker, and it exists. If it is said that it died with this agreement, we say this is subsidiary to the authority of the agreement, and discussion on it follows. Understand this. Then Imam Abu Hanifa, in one narration, held that the sale of Umm Walad by a judge's ruling is valid, contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. So it is said: this is based on the view that previous disagreement prevents later consensus; otherwise, the consensus of the Followers on impermissibility would have occurred, and a ruling contradicting consensus is not valid. So the author intended to refute this and said: 'And what is narrated from Abu Hanifa in non-zahir narrations about the validity of the sale of Umm Walad contrary to the two, as in al-Mizan, and Shams al-A'imma mentioned that Abu Yusuf sold [with Abu Hanifa], because the issue is ijtihadi concerning the authority of this consensus. So for one who considers this consensus authoritative, the ruling is not valid; for one who does not, it is valid. Thus its validity is disputed; it is valid if ratification is found.'
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage addresses a key usul dispute: can a later generation of mujtahids form a binding consensus on a matter that was disputed by earlier mujtahids? The author presents the view of al-Ash'ari, Ahmad, al-Ghazali, and al-Juwayni that it is impossible, while the majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is hold that it can occur and is authoritative. Evidence is provided from the practice of the Followers (Tabi'un) on two issues: Mut'at al-Hajj and selling Umm Walad. The Followers are said to have been unanimous on the permissibility of Mut'at al-Hajj despite earlier disagreement among the Companions (e.g., 'Uthman forbade it, but 'Ali and others practiced it). The author defends this consensus against objections: the prohibition by 'Umar is not authentically reported, and 'Uthman's prohibition is countered by 'Ali's practice. The discussion on Umm Walad shows that although the Companions differed, the Followers reached consensus on prohibition; however, the author notes that this consensus is not reliably established. The passage also ties to a fiqh issue: Abu Hanifa's view that a judge's sale of Umm Walad could be valid, which is based on the view that the earlier disagreement prevents later consensus from being binding. The author concludes that the matter is ijtihadi, so the ruling's validity depends on which view is taken.

Key Terms
العصر الثاني (al-'asr al-thani): The second generation of mujtahids after the Companions, i.e., the Followers (Tabi'un).
متعة الحج (mut'at al-hajj): Performing 'Umrah and Hajj in one journey with two separate ihrams during the Hajj months, also called Tamattu'.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has borne a child from her master, becoming free upon his death.
ممتنع (mumtani'): Impossible or impermissible in the sense of being logically or legally impossible to occur.
حجة (hujja): A binding proof or argument in legal reasoning.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred position according to the author of the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the consensus of the Followers on the prohibition of selling Umm Walad?
A) It is firmly established and accepted by all schools.
B) It is not reliably established and has not been transmitted in a sound manner.
C) It was contested by the Companions but accepted by the Followers.
D) It was unanimously accepted by the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
Later consensus after earlier disagreement is possible and authoritative according to the majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is, with practical consequences for many fiqh rulings.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced
15 min
The Authority of Later Consensus vs. Prior Ijtihad
Refutes sahabi consensus claims and discusses ijma's effect on prior views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a later consensus does not automatically abrogate an earlier valid mujtahid's opinion, and identify when earlier opinions remain valid despite a claimed consensus.

Core Idea
A later consensus cannot override an earlier valid ijtihad unless a definitive text emerges.

Scholars sometimes claim that a consensus (ijma') later emerged on a ruling that contradicts an earlier mujtahid's opinion. Does this invalidate the earlier view? This lesson examines a critical debate in Hanafi usul: whether a later consensus nullifies prior valid ijtihad, using the examples of mut'ah of Hajj and the sale of umm walad. You will learn the Hanafi stance that the authority of such consensuses is itself disputed, and that earlier opinions based on strong evidence remain authoritative for those who held them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed consensuses
The passage discusses claims of consensus among the Tabi'un on the permissibility of mut'ah al-Hajj and the impermissibility of selling an umm walad. Identify each claim and its basis.
The mut'ah claim is based on widespread practice; the umm walad claim is said to be unproven.
2
Analyze the objection to the umm walad consensus
The author argues that the consensus on umm walad sale is not reliably established. Why does he reject it? Look for his critique of the transmission.
He says it is not transmitted in a way acceptable to reason and the canons of authenticity.
3
Examine the Hanafi principle on later consensus
The author defends that a later consensus does not automatically invalidate an earlier valid ijtihad. Why? Because the earlier opinion survives through its evidence (dalil), not through the person.
The survival of evidence means the opinion remains valid unless a qati' text emerges.
4
Consider the intra-Hanafi difference on umm walad sale
Abu Hanifa reportedly allowed a judge's ruling to execute the sale, contradicting the claimed consensus. How is this explained?
The issue is ijtihadi: those who reject the consensus authority allow the sale; those who accept it do not.
5
Respond to the objection of 'declaring Companions misguided'
If the later consensus is valid, does it declare earlier Companions misguided? The author says no: their opinion was based on valid evidence at the time; they only erred after the consensus, but error in ijtihad is not sin.
This upholds the respect for earlier mujtahids while maintaining that truth is one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثالث الإجماع أمير المؤمنين (عثمان ينهي عنه أما نهي أمير المؤمنين عثمان فثابت في «الصحيحين»، وغيره في الحاشية في صحيح البخاري أن مروان قال : شهدت عثمان وعلياً وعثمان ينهي عن المتعة وأن يجمع بينهما، فلما رأى علي أهل بهما : لبيك بعمرة وحجة وقال : ما كنت لأدع سنة النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لقول أحد، ثم الروايات متظافرة، فلا يضر كون الراوي مروان، وأما نهي أمير المؤمنين عمر فلم يثبت بسند صحيح، لكن يروى في غير المعتبرات أن كان يقول : ثلاث كن على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه عمر وسلم أنا أحرمهن وأنهي عنهن متعة الحج ومتعة النكاح وحي على خير العمل فإن صح فمعناه أن الثلاثة التي وقعت في العهد الشريف أحياناً أنا أبين حرمتهن التي تبنت منه عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام وأنهي عنهن لأجل الحرمة الثابتة في الشرع الشريف بعد الإباحة وأراد بمتعة الحج فسخ الحج بالعمرة، ثم الحج بالإحرام في يوم قبل عرفة فإنه وإن وقع في حجة أحد الوداع لكنه كان مختصاً بالصحابة كما قال أبو ذر رواه مسلم وهذا موافق لما عنه في روي الصحيحين أنه قال لعلي أن الله يقول: ﴿ وَأَتِمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلهِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٩٦] جميعاً وأما رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فقد ساق الهدي فلم يحل. وأما متعة النساء وإن أبيحت يوم خيبر لكن حرمت بعد ذلك إلى يوم القيامة وحي على خير العمل قد نسخ في العهد الشريف، ولهذا تواتر الآذان،بدونه، وإنما وصف الثلاثة بكونهن في العهد الشريف رداً لمن يتوهم الجواز بسماع أنها كانت فأزال الوهم بأنها وإن كانت لكن لم تبق عليكم فافهم، وإنما آثرنا نوعاً من الأطناب لأن بعض السفهاء من الروافض يطفئون نور الله بأفواههم ويقولون : إن أمير المؤمنين حرم ما كان مباحاً في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وهو كبيرة فلا يلتفت إليه (و) لنا إجماع التابعين على عدم جواز بيع أم الولد وقد اختلفت الصحابة فيه إجماع التابعين على جواز متعة الحج لعله واضح فإنهم كانوا معلومين عرف منهم عمل التمتع والفتوى به في أيام الحج لاجتماعهم فيها وأما إجماعهم على حرمة بيع أم الولد فلم يصح بعد ولم ينقل بوجه يقبله العقل وقوانين الصحة (وأما الحجية) أي حجية هذا الإجماع (فلئلا يلزم خلو الزمان عن الحق واتفاق الأمة على الخطأ المنفي عنهم بالنص (وفيه ما فيه) لأن خلو الزمان عن الحق ممنوع وإنما يلزم لو لم يكن قول المجتهد الأول باقياً، وهو في حيز الخفاء، فإنّ بقاءه ببقاء الدليل لا ببقاء القائل وهو موجود، وإن قيل قد مات بهذا الاتفاق قلنا هذا فرع حجية الاتفاق وفيه الكلام بعد فافهم. ثم إن الإمام أبا حنيفة ذهب في رواية إلى نفاذ بيع أم الولد بحكم القاضي خلافاً لهما فقيل : هذا مبني على أن الخلاف السابق يمنع الإجماع اللاحق وإلا فقد انعقد إجماع التابعين على عدم الجواز والقضاء مخالف الإجماع لا ينفذ، فأراد المصنف دفع هذا القول وقال (وما) روي عن أبي حنيفة في غير الظاهر) من الرواية (من نفاذ القضاء أم الولد خلافاً لهما على ما في «الميزان»، وذكر شمس الأئمة أن أبا يوسف ببيع مع أبي حنيفة فلأن المسألة مسألة حجية هذا الإجماع (اجتهادية) فعند من يرى هذا الإجماع حجة لم ينفذ القضاء وعند من يرى عدم الحجية ينفذ فنفاذه مختلف فيه فينفذ إذا وجد إمضاء قاض آخر وهو محمل رواية النفاذ لأنه الحكم في كل قضاء مختلف فيه فافهم. فإن قلت: لو اعتبر هذا الإجماع لزم تضليل بعض الصحابة الذين وقع الإجماع على خلاف قولهم لأن مخالفة الإجماع ضلالة، أجاب وقال : (ولا) يلزم تضليل بعض الصحابة، لأن رأيه كان حجة قبل حدوث الإجماع فحكمه كان عن دليل شرعي موجب للعمل وإنما تقاعد بعد الإجماع لظهور نص خلاف حكمه بعده (وإنما اللازم خطؤه وهو لازم في كل اختلاف لأن الحق واحد فتأمل)
The third principle: Consensus. Amir al-Mu'minin 'Uthman forbids it. As for the prohibition of 'Uthman, it is established in the Sahihayn, and elsewhere in the commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari that Marwan said: I witnessed 'Uthman and 'Ali, and 'Uthman was forbidding mut'ah and combining them. When 'Ali saw him, he said: 'Labbayk with 'Umrah and Hajj' and said: 'I would not abandon the sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ for the saying of anyone.' Then the narrations are numerous, so it does not harm that the narrator is Marwan. As for the prohibition of 'Umar, it is not established with a sound chain, but it is narrated in non-reliable sources that he used to say: 'Three were during the time of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and I prohibit them and forbid them: mut'ah of Hajj, mut'ah of women, and Hayya 'ala khayr al-'amal.' If authentic, its meaning is that these three occurred at times in the noble era; I clarify their prohibition which was established from him ﷺ after permissibility and forbid them due to the established prohibition in the noble Shari'ah after permissibility. He intended by mut'ah of Hajj the annulment of Hajj to 'Umrah, then Hajj with Ihram on a day before 'Arafah; for although it occurred in the Farewell Hajj, it was specific to the Companions as Abu Dharr said (Muslim narrated it). This is consistent with what is reported in the Sahihayn that he said to 'Ali: 'Allah says: Complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' together; and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ drove the sacrificial animal so he did not become permissible. As for mut'ah of women, although it was permitted on the day of Khaybar, it was later prohibited until the Day of Judgment. 'Hayya 'ala khayr al-'amal' was abrogated in the noble era; hence the Adhan is consistently performed without it. He only described the three as being in the noble era as a refutation against those who imagine permissibility by hearing that they existed; he removed the illusion saying they existed but did not remain for you. Understand. We have preferred a kind of prolixity because some foolish Rafidah extinguish the light of Allah with their mouths and say: 'The Commander of the Faithful prohibited what was permissible in the era of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and that is a grave sin.' So it is not heeded. (And) we have the consensus of the Tabi'un on the impermissibility of selling an umm walad, while the Companions differed on it. Consensus of the Tabi'un on the permissibility of mut'ah of Hajj is perhaps clear, for they were known, and the practice of tamattu' and fatwa on it was observed during the days of Hajj due to their gathering. As for their consensus on the prohibition of selling umm walad, it is not established, nor is it transmitted in a way acceptable to reason and the canons of authenticity. (And as for the authority) i.e., the authority of this consensus, (it is) 'lest the age be devoid of truth and the ummah agree on error, which is negated from them by the text.' (But there is something in it) because the absence of the age from truth is denied; it would only follow if the statement of the first mujtahid were not remaining, and it is in the realm of hiddenness. For its survival is by the survival of the evidence, not by the survival of the speaker, and it exists. If it is said it has died with this agreement, we say: This is a branch of the authority of agreement, and the discussion is after this. Understand. Then Imam Abu Hanifa went in one narration to the execution of the sale of umm walad by a judge's ruling, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). So it is said: This is based on that prior disagreement prevents later consensus; otherwise, the consensus of the Tabi'un on non-permissibility has occurred, and a ruling contradicting consensus is not executed. So the author intended to refute this saying and said: (And what) is narrated from Abu Hanifa in non-zahir (narration) (of the execution of the judgment on umm walad contrary to the two, as in 'al-Mizan', and Shams al-A'immah mentioned that Abu Yusuf sold with Abu Hanifa. For the issue is a matter of the authority of this consensus (Ijtihadi). So according to one who regards this consensus as authoritative, the judgment is not executed; according to one who does not regard authority, it is executed. So its execution is disputed; thus it is executed if there is ratification by another judge, and that is the interpretation of the narration of execution, because it is the ruling in every disputed judgment. Understand. If you say: If we consider this consensus, it would necessitate declaring some Companions misguided, because opposing consensus is misguidance. He answered and said: (And it does) not necessitate declaring some Companions misguided, because his opinion was an authority before the occurrence of consensus, so his ruling was based on a Shar'i evidence requiring action; it only fell away after consensus due to the emergence of a text contradicting his ruling afterwards. (And what is necessary is his error, and that is necessary in every difference, because the truth is one. So reflect.)
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a detailed polemical discussion about the validity of claimed consensuses (ijma') on three issues: mut'ah of Hajj, mut'ah of women, and the call 'Hayya 'ala khayr al-'amal', as well as the sale of umm walad. The author first addresses objections that these consensuses are not proven or are based on weak evidence. He distinguishes between the claim of consensus among the Companions and that among the Tabi'un. For mut'ah of Hajj, he argues that the practice of tamattu' was common among the Tabi'un, so their consensus on its permissibility is plausible, but the prohibition of selling umm walad is not reliably transmitted. The core debate is whether later consensus can override earlier differing opinions of mujtahids. The author defends the Hanafi position that a later consensus does not necessarily nullify the earlier view because the earlier view remains valid based on its own evidence (dalil) until a definitive text (nass qati') emerges. He also discusses the internal Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa reportedly allowed a judge's ruling to execute the sale of umm walad, even if it contradicts a later consensus, because that consensus is not absolutely authoritative. The author clarifies that this is an ijtihadi issue; thus different views exist, and the ruling of a judge is enforceable if ratified by another judge. Finally, he addresses the objection that accepting this consensus would require declaring earlier Companions misguided. He responds that their opinion was valid before the consensus; after consensus, they may be in error, but that does not imply sin, as the truth is one and error is inevitable in ijtihad. The passage orders: present the claim, analyze evidence, refute objections, and conclude with the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah on a legal ruling.
متعة الحج (mut'ah al-hajj): Performing 'Umrah and Hajj separately during the Hajj season with a break of ihram between them, also called tamattu'.
أم الولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the consensus of the Tabi'un on the impermissibility of selling umm walad not necessarily invalidate the earlier differing opinion of Abu Hanifa?
A) Because Abu Hanifa's opinion is based on a definitive text
B) Because the consensus is not proven to have occurred
C) Because the authority (hujjiyya) of that consensus is itself disputed, so the issue is ijtihadi
D) Because Abu Hanifa's opinion was later ratified by a judge

Key Takeaway
A later consensus does not automatically abrogate earlier valid ijtihad; the survival of the evidence keeps the earlier opinion authoritative unless a definitive text emerges.
