خاتمة في الاجتهاد والتقليد (مسألة: لا يجوز التقليد في العقليات كوجود الباري : ونحوه عند الأكثر) وهذا لا ينافي مر من إجماع الأئمة الأربعة على صحة إيمان :المقلد : لأن التقليد الممنوع هو أن يعتمد على قول الغير فيقول بحسب قوله وهذا لا ينافي صحة الإيمان والتصديق إذا وجد بقوله، لكن رسخ بحيث لو ذهب قوله من البين لبقي هو على التصديق فافهم والعنبري وبعض الشافعية) قالوا : (يجوز) التقليد فيها (وطائفة) قالوا : (يجب التقليد ( ويحرم النظر لنا : الاجماع القاطع على وجوب العلم بالله وصفاته ورسالة رسوله، وهو التصديق الجازم المطابق، بحيث لا يقبل التشكيك أصلاً ولا يحصل بالتقليد لإمكان كذب المخبر لكونه غير معصوم، نعم: إن حدث بعد التقليد تصديق جازم كما يحدث نتيجة قاطعة عن مقدمات مشهورة ثم يذهل عنها ويبقى تصديقها يقبل، ولأنه يلزم النقيضان في تقليد اثنين في حدوث العالم وقدمه مثلاً لكون كل منهما علماً فلا بد من النظر الصحيح ليحصل العلم، وهذا إنما يتم لو قلنا: إن كل تقليد يفيد العلم، بل مجوز والتقليد لعل مطمح نظرهم أن التقليد قد يفيد الجزم، ثم إن كان مقلداً لمن له علم واقعي يكون جزمه علماً، فقد حصل بتقليد بعض الكملة العلم القاطع، ولعل إنكار هذا إنكار للقطعيات بل الحق في هذا المقام الواجب تحصيل العلم فقط، وهو قد يحصل بصفاء السريرة ضرورة، فلا يجب عليه النظر قطعاً كما حكى الشيخ الأكبر صاحب «الفتوحات» قدس سره عن أفضل الصديقين بعد الأنبياء عليهم السلام وسيد المتقين إمام الأولياء بالتحقيق أمير المؤمنين أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله تعالى عنه، وقد يحصل للبعض بتقليد من يعلمه أعلى منه، ولا يحتاج هذا إلى النظر لكن إن نظر كان أولى، وقد يحصل بنظر ، وهذا أكثر في الرجال، فالنظر واجب عليهم فقط فافهم وتثبت مجوزو التقليد :(قالوا :لو وجب النظر لفعله الصحابة وأمروا به، وذلك منتف وإلا نقل كما في الفروع بل دواعي هذا النقل أوفر لاشتغال كل أحد .به قلنا لو لم يكن النظر (منهم) لزم نسبتهم إلى الجهل بالله وصفاته بوجه، وهو باطل إجماعاً وضرورة من الدين فإذن هم نظروا وأمروا به (وأما النقل ففرع الإكثار من النظر والبحث على ما هو وظيفة الكلام وهم كانوا مستغنين عن الإكثار والاشتغال بالبحث (بصفاء الأذهان ومشاهدة الوحي، ولا نسلم عدم الأمر ) أي عدم أمرهم لمن تبعهم (لكنهم كانوا عالمين بحصوله) للتابعين (فإنه ليس المراد بالنظر ههنا (تحرير الأدلة على قواعد المنطق) فإنه ليس التصديق موقوفاً إلا للبعض الأندر (بل) المراد (ما يفيد الطمأنينة) للقلب بحيث يصير أطوع لحصول العلم (كما قال الأعرابي : البعرة تدل على البعير، وأثر الاقدام على المسير، فسماء ذات أبراج وأرض ذات فجاج، أما يدلان على اللطيف الخبير وحاصل الجواب منع عدم نظرهم بالكلية، ومنع عدم ،أمرهم فإن المراد بالنظر قدر ما يطمئن به القلب بحصول التصديق، وهو كان حاصلاً لهم كما يشهد به قصة الأعرابي، وأما دعوى أنه لو لم يكن منهم لزم الجهل بوجه فغير ظاهر الصحة فإن كمال استعدادهم وتوجه الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لعلهما يوجبان العلم الضروري.
حكاية لطيفة ) : أن رجلاً من البدلاء مات في أرض الشام أو الروم، فذهب قطب الوقت الشيخ محيي الدين عبد القادر الجيلاني قدس سره الشريف في ساعة أو في نصف ساعة، وكان قدس سره في أرض العراق، وحضر أبو العباس الخضر عليه السلام، والبدلاء الآخرون، فصلى عليه ودفنه، وأمر الخضر أن يأتي رجلاً وسماه له من القسطنطينية، وكان هو كافراً غليظاً، فأتى به الخضر عنده، فلقنه الشيخ كلمتي الشهادتين وقص الشوارب، وأوصله إلى مقام البدلاء وأقامه مقام الميت وأخبر البدلاء الحاضرين فقالوا : سمعاً وطاعة، وقد تواتر أمثال هذه الحكايات منه رضي الله تعالى عنه تواتراً معنوياً، فانظر بعين الإنصاف أين كان ههنا النظر إنما حدث في قلبه علم ضروري. موجبو التقليد (قالوا : النظر مظنة الوقوع في الشبه (والضلال فإن طريق النظر غير آمن والتقليد طريق آمن فلا بد من إيجابه (قلنا هذا (منقوض بالمقلد) على صيغة المفعول، أي قلد من به فإنه غير مقلد للغير ( وإلا) يكن كذلك، بل كان هو مقلداً أيضاً (تسلسل، لأن الأخذ عن المؤيد بالوحي ليس تقليداً، بل) هو (علم نظري) فلو كان المقلد به مقلداً لكان له مقلد به أيضاً هذا وفيه نوع شبهة، فإنه يجوز أن تنتهي السلسلة إلى الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، ولا نسلم أن المأخوذ منه علم ،نظري، بل يكون ضرورياً حاصلاً من بركة الصحبة الشريفة، والأولى في الجواب أن يقال : ليس التقليد طريقاً إلى تحصيل العلم اليقيني وإن كان قد يحصل به أيضاً بخلاف النظر فإنه إذا وقع في مقدمات مقطوعة لزم حصول العلم، وإنما يكون غير مأمون بتقصير منه كإنكار البديهيات وغيره فافهم .
Conclusion on Ijtihad and Taqlid. Issue: Taqlid is not permissible in intellectual matters such as the existence of God and similar topics according to the majority. This does not contradict the earlier mention of the consensus of the four imams on the validity of the faith of the muqallid, because the prohibited taqlid is to rely on the statement of another and say according to his statement, and this does not contradict the validity of faith and attestation if it occurs by his statement, but firmly established such that if the statement of the other were removed, he would remain in attestation. So understand. Al-Anbari and some Shafi'is said: it is permissible. And a group said: it is obligatory to perform taqlid and it is prohibited to engage in nazar. Our proof: the conclusive consensus on the obligation of knowledge of Allah, His attributes, and the message of His messenger, which is firm and correct attestation that does not accept any doubt at all, and it is not attained by taqlid because of the possibility of the informer lying as he is not infallible. Yes, if after taqlid a firm attestation occurs as a conclusive result from well-known premises and then one forgets them and the attestation remains, it is accepted. And because the two contradictories would follow in taqlid of two persons on the eternity and creation of the world, for example, since each would be a proof, so sound nazar is necessary to attain knowledge. This is only valid if we say that every taqlid yields knowledge, but rather permissive. And perhaps the intention of those who permit taqlid is that taqlid may yield conviction, then if one is a muqallid of someone who has real knowledge, his conviction becomes knowledge. So by taqlid of some perfected ones, conclusive knowledge may be attained. Perhaps denial of this is denial of certainties. Rather the truth in this place is that only the acquisition of knowledge is obligatory, and it may occur by purity of inner conscience necessarily, so nazar is not obligatory upon him definitively, as related by the great shaykh, the author of al-Futuhat, may his secret be sanctified, from the best of the truthful after the prophets, peace be upon them, and the master of the pious, the imam of the saints, the commander of the faithful, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. And it may occur for some by taqlid of someone they know to be above them, and this does not need nazar, but if he perform nazar it is better. And it may occur by nazar, and this is more common among men, so nazar is obligatory only upon them. So understand. Those who permit taqlid said: if nazar were obligatory, the Companions would have done it and commanded it, and that is not transmitted; otherwise it would have been transmitted as in the furu'. Rather the motives for transmission are greater because everyone is occupied with it. We say: if nazar were not from them, it would lead to attributing ignorance of Allah and His attributes to them, which is false by consensus and necessity of religion. Therefore, they did nazar and commanded it. As for transmission, it is a branch of abundant nazar and research according to the function of kalam, and they were independent of abundance and being occupied with research due to purity of minds and witnessing of revelation. And we do not concede the lack of command, i.e., their command to those who followed them, but they knew it would occur for the followers. For the intended nazar here is not the verification of proofs according to logical rules, for attestation is not dependent except for the rare few, but rather the intended meaning is that which gives tranquility to the heart such that it becomes more obedient in attaining knowledge, as the Bedouin said: The dung indicates the camel, and the footprints indicate the journey, so a sky with constellations and an earth with valleys—do they not indicate the Subtle and Aware? The conclusion of the answer is the denial of their lack of nazar entirely, and the denial of their lack of command, for the intended nazar is the amount that gives tranquility to the heart in attaining attestation, and that was present for them as witnessed by the story of the Bedouin. As for the claim that if it were not from them it would lead to ignorance in some way, it is not clearly valid, for their perfect preparedness and the attention of the Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and his Companions perhaps necessitate necessary knowledge. A delightful story: A man from the abdāl died in the land of Syria or Rome, so the Qutb of the time, Shaykh Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, may his noble secret be sanctified, went in an hour or half an hour, and he was in the land of Iraq. And Abu al-Abbas al-Khidr, peace be upon him, and the other abdāl attended, and he prayed over him and buried him. And he commanded al-Khidr to bring a man named by him from Constantinople, and he was a coarse disbeliever. So al-Khidr brought him to him. The shaykh taught him the two testimonies and trimmed his mustache, and elevated him to the station of the abdāl and placed him in the place of the deceased. The present abdāl said: hearing and obedience. Similar stories from him, may Allah be pleased with him, have been mutawatir in meaning. Look with the eye of fairness: where was nazar here? Only necessary knowledge occurred in his heart. Those who obligate taqlid said: nazar is a place for falling into doubts and misguidance, for the path of nazar is not safe, while taqlid is a safe path, so it must be obligatory. We say: this is overturned by the muqallad (passive form), i.e., the one who is followed, for he is not a muqallid of others. If not so, but rather he was also a muqallid, it would lead to infinite regress, because taking from the one supported by revelation is not taqlid, but rather theoretical knowledge. So if the muqallad were a muqallid, he would also have a muqallad, etc. This contains some doubt, for it is possible that the chain ends with the Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and we do not concede that the taken from is theoretical knowledge, but rather it is necessary knowledge obtained from the blessing of noble companionship. The better answer is to say: taqlid is not a path to attaining certain knowledge, even if it may also be attained by it, unlike nazar, for if it falls into conclusive premises, knowledge necessarily occurs, and it is only unsafe due to shortcoming from him, like denial of self-evident truths and so on. So understand.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the ruling of taqlid in intellectual matters ('aqliyat) such as belief in God. The author presents the positions of different groups: the majority (including the Hanafi school) prohibit it, al-Anbari and some Shafi'is permit it, and a third group make it obligatory while prohibiting independent reasoning (nazar). The Hanafi proof is based on the conclusive consensus (ijma' qati') that knowledge of God and His attributes must be certain and cannot rely on fallible human testimony. Taqlid does not produce certain knowledge because the informer could be lying. However, if after taqlid a firm conviction arises that matches reality, it becomes valid. The author then explains that the Companions did engage in nazar, but their nazar was simple reflection that brought tranquility, not formal logical argument. A story of Shaykh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani illustrates that necessary knowledge can occur without formal reasoning. The passage also addresses the objection that if nazar leads to doubt, taqlid is safer. The response is that the one being followed (muqallad) himself is not a muqallid but has knowledge, so there is no infinite regress. Ultimately, taqlid is not a reliable path to certainty, but nazar when properly done leads to knowledge.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Relying on the statement of another without knowing its proof or being able to verify it independently.
عقليات ('aqliyat): Intellectual matters that require rational proof, such as belief in God, prophethood, and the afterlife.
نظر (nazar): Rational inquiry or reflection aimed at acquiring knowledge; in this passage, specifically the kind that produces tranquility and certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority (including the Hanafi school), what is the ruling on performing taqlid in intellectual matters such as the existence of God?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is permissible
C) It is not permissible
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Taqlid in intellectual matters is not permissible for attaining the required certain knowledge, but if it accidentally leads to firm conviction, the faith is valid; the ideal path is nazar that brings tranquility to the heart.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
6 min
Permissibility of Issuing Fatwas through Takhrij
Establishes permissibility of fatwa by takhrij via consensus and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi evidence for the permissibility of takhrij and apply the concept of implicit ijma to defend a usul position.

Core Idea
Fatwa by takhrij is permissible for deeply learned scholars, established by the silent consensus of the mujtahid era.

This lesson examines a key usul al-fiqh passage that defends the practice of takhrij (deriving rulings within a madhhab) by scholars who are not independent mujtahids. The author argues that such fatwa is supported by implicit consensus (ijma sukuti) from the silence of earlier mujtahids and by the continuous practice of verifying scholars. We will analyze the evidence and refute the objection that would equate such scholars with laymen.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
What is the ruling being argued? The permissibility of a non-mujtahid scholar issuing fatwa by takhrij. The Hanafi position affirms it for deeply learned scholars (mutabahhirun).
Distinguish between a mutabahhir and a layman.
2
Analyze the primary evidence: implicit consensus
The passage cites that Hanafi followers gave fatwas in the time of Imam al-Shafi'i and others without rejection. This silence constitutes ijma sukuti. Identify the elements: presence of mujtahids, occurrence of the practice, absence of objection.
Consensus is zanni due to its implicit nature.
3
Examine the objector's qiyas and the Hanafi response
The objector analogizes the scholar to a layman: if both know the evidence, both should be allowed. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the scholar can assess counter-evidence (mu'āriḍ), the layman cannot. This breaks the analogy.
The ruling depends on awareness of counter-evidence.
4
Evaluate the strength of the evidence
The primary evidence (ijma sukuti) is zanni in both transmission and meaning, but it is reinforced by the continuous agreement of scholars across ages. The refutation of the qiyas objection adds rational support.
The passage does not claim certainty, but sufficient proof for practice.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a mutabahhir scholar may issue fatwas by takhrij; otherwise, only full mujtahids may. The Hanafi school allows it, while some stricter views restrict it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز أصلاً (وأما النقل لقولهم : المنصوص ( كالأحاديث) أي كنقلها (فاتفاق) في الجواز، ويقبل بشرائط الرواية إن لم يكن متواتراً، وإلا فيقبل مطلقاً لنا) وقوعه) أي الإفتاء المذكور تخريجاً (من) العلماء المتبحرين في جميع الأعصار بلا نكير وينكر) الافتاء تخريجاً (من غيرهم) أي غير المتبحرين (فكان إجماعاً على جوازه لهم دون غيرهم (قيل: إذ فرض عدم المجتهدين فلا إجماع) لأن أهله المجتهدون (وأجيب باعتبار التجزي) يعني الاجتهاد متجز والعلماء الأعلام في كل عصر أفتوا زعماً منهم بجواز هذا الافتاء اجتهاداً فتأمل فيه (أقول: وأيضاً وقع هذا الافتاء في زمان المجتهدين فإن أصحاب الإمام أبي حنيفة كانوا يفتون بمذهبه في (زمان الإمام الشافعي و الإمام (أحمد) وغيرهما، كابن معين وابن عيينة وعطاء وغيرهم بلا نكير من أحد فكان هذا إجماعاً ( وحينئذ ) أي حين جاز عند وجودهم (جاز عند عدمهم بذلك الإجماع أو بطريق أولى فإذا جاز عند وجود من يمكن الاستفتاء منه فعند عدمهم يجوز بالطريق الأولى على أن اتفاق العلماء المحققين على ممر الأعصار) وإن كانوا غير مجتهدين (حجة) كالاجماع فإنه يأبى العقل من اجتماعهم من غير أن يكون واضحاً لديهم وإنه كان بالسماع عن مجتهديهم . قال : المانع لو جاز) لعالم الجاز لعامي إذا عرف) هو أيضاً حكم) حادثة بدليله كما أن العالم يعلم كذلك فهما سواء، ولا يجوز للعامي بالاتفاق، فلا يجوز للعالم أيضاً قلنا : الحكم موقوف على عدم المعارض وهو) أي العامي (غير عالم) به فلا علم لديه بدليله بخلاف العالم.
It is permissible originally. As for transmission, they say: the textually stated (like hadiths), i.e., like their transmission, is agreed upon in permissibility, and is accepted under the conditions of narration if not mutawatir; otherwise it is accepted absolutely. For us, its occurrence—meaning the aforementioned fatwa by takhrij—from the deeply learned scholars in all ages without any rejection [supports] that it is consensus upon its permissibility for them, not for others. It is said: if we assume absence of mujtahids, then there is no consensus because its people are mujtahids. It was answered by considering partial ijtihad, meaning ijtihad is divisible, and the great scholars in every age gave fatwas, supposing the permissibility of this fatwa by ijtihad, so reflect on it. I say: also this fatwa occurred in the time of mujtahids, for the companions of Imam Abu Hanifa used to give fatwas according to his madhhab in the time of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad, and others—like Ibn Ma'in, Ibn 'Uyayna, 'Ata' and others—without any rejection from anyone, so this was consensus. And then, i.e., when it was permissible in their presence, it becomes permissible in their absence by that consensus or by a primary argument. So if it is permissible in the presence of those from whom fatwa can be sought, then in their absence it is permissible by primary argument. Moreover, the agreement of the verifying scholars over the ages, even if they are not mujtahids, is a proof like consensus, because reason repels their gathering without it being clear to them and that it was by hearing from their mujtahids. The objector said: If it is permissible for a scholar, it would be permissible for a layman if he knows a ruling of an incident by its evidence, just as the scholar knows it, so both are equal, and it is not permissible for a layman by consensus, so it is not permissible for the scholar either. We said: The ruling depends on the absence of a counter-evidence, and the layman is not aware of that, so he has no knowledge of its evidence, unlike the scholar.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut comments on a matn concerning the permissibility of issuing fatwas through takhrij (derivation) by scholars who are not independent mujtahids. The author begins by affirming that such fatwa is permissible in principle, and draws an analogy to the transmission of hadith: transmitted texts are accepted with conditions unless mutawatir, in which case they are accepted absolutely. The primary evidence is that deeply learned scholars (al-mutabahhirun) in every era have issued fatwas via takhrij without disapproval, which constitutes implicit consensus (ijma) on its permissibility for them. A objection is raised: if there are no mujtahids, there can be no consensus. The author responds that ijtihad can be partial (tajzi), and the great scholars in each age claimed the authority to give such fatwas, so it iﬁs an issue of ijtihad. The author adds that this fatwa by takhrij actually occurred in the time of full mujtahids—for example, the followers of Abu Hanifa gave fatwas according to his madhhab while al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and others were alive, without any rejection. This silence from the mujtahids of that era constitutes clear consensus. Consequently, if it was valid in their presence, it is even more valid in their absence (by a fortiori argument). Finally, an objector argues that if a scholar can do takhrij, a layman who knows the evidence can too, and since the layman cannot, the scholar cannot. The author refutes this by distinguishing: the scholar's ruling is based on awareness of counter-evidence, which the layman lacks.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): The process of deriving rulings from the principles and texts of a specific madhhab by a scholar who is not an independent mujtahid.
متبحر (mutabahhir): A deeply learned scholar who has mastered the shar'i sciences, capable of takhrij even if not a full mujtahid.
اجتهاد متجزئ (ijtihad mutajazzi): Partial ijtihad, referring to the ability to derive rulings in some areas but not all, often associated with takhrij.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used to justify fatwa through takhrij in this passage?
A) Direct Quranic text
B) Sunnah of the Prophet
C) Implicit consensus from the silence of earlier mujtahids
D) Logical necessity

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of takhrij for deeply learned scholars is established by implicit consensus and the continuous practice of the Hanafi school.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
advanced
8 min
Can Ijma' Override a Khabar Wahid?
Usul dispute on ijma' and khabar wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi position on when ijma' can contradict a khabar wahid and evaluate the counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ijma' can override a khabar wahid if the report is weak or possibly abrogated.

A khabar wahid (isolated report) is a zanni (probable) proof. Ijma' is qat'i (definitive). Can later consensus contradict a ruling derived from an isolated hadith? Some argue that the very existence of the khabar prevents ijma' because it counts as a dissenting opinion. This lesson examines the Hanafi response: the khabar may be abrogated or weak, and if definitively established, ijma' cannot override it. But otherwise, consensus can supersede it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the contested issue: Can ijma' be validly concluded contrary to a khabar wahid?
2
Analyze the objection
Understand the opposing argument: the khabar itself constitutes a dissenting opinion, so no true consensus can exist.
This objection relies on the definition of ijma' requiring unanimity.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The author refutes by noting that the khabar may be abrogated or weak. If abrogated, its ruling no longer applies, so consensus is possible. If weak, it is not a valid dissent.
Abrogation (naskh) can occur without the abrogator being preserved.
4
Distinguish qat'i from zanni
If the khabar is definitively established (qat'i al-thubut) and its ruling remains, then ijma' cannot contradict it. Otherwise, ijma' can override.
This preserves the hierarchy: qat'i overrides zanni.
5
Apply the principle
Conclude that ijma' overrides the khabar because the agreement of an era is infallible. Without consensus, the earlier statement remains valid for taqlid.
The principle: 'جماعة لا تجتمع على ضلالة' - the community does not agree on error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة في الاجتهاد والتقليد الإجماع على خلافه لوجود قول مخالف (أقول : منقوض بالخبر لجواز انعقاده بخلافه) وفيه أنه لا نقض، فإنّ الخبر قابل للنسخ فيحتمل أن يكون منسوخاً في الواقع ولم يحفظ ناسخه، فيمكن أن ينعقد على خلافه الإجماع، أو يكون ضعيفاً غير ثابت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأما إذا ثبت قطعاً وعلم بقاء حكمه، التزم عدم جواز انعقاد الإجماع على خلافه، وأما ههنا فلو اعتبر قول الميت لم يكن اتفاق المجتهدين اللاحقين كلهم على خلافه إجماعاً، لأن القول المخالف موجود، فالحق في الجواب أن يقال إنه قد علم من الشرع أن اتفاق عصر ما لا يكون خطأ، فالإجماع مميت له، فلذا يصح انعقاد الإجماع على خلافه، وما لم يتحقق الإجماع فقوله حي دليله، فيصح تقليده.
Conclusion on ijtihad and taqlid. The consensus contrary to it due to the existence of a dissenting opinion. (I say: It is rebutted by the khabar because it is possible for consensus to be concluded contrary to it.) But there is no rebuttal, for the khabar is susceptible to abrogation; it is possible that it was abrogated in reality but its abrogator was not preserved, so consensus may be concluded contrary to it, or it may be weak and not authentically established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). However, if it is definitively established and its ruling is known to remain, then the lack of permissibility of concluding consensus contrary to it is upheld. But here, if the statement of the deceased were considered, the agreement of all later mujtahids contrary to it would not be consensus, because the dissenting statement exists. The correct answer is to say: It is known from the Shari'ah that the agreement of a particular era cannot be erroneous, so consensus overrides it. Therefore, it is valid to conclude consensus contrary to it. As long as consensus is not realized, his statement is alive as his evidence, so his taqlid is valid.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the possibility of ijma' (consensus) contradicting a khabar wahid (isolated report). The author presents an objection: that ijma' cannot be validly formed against a khabar wahid because the existence of the khabar counts as a dissenting opinion. He refutes this by arguing that the khabar may be abrogated or weak, and if it is definitively established and unnabrogated, then ijma' cannot contradict it. The correct answer, he says, is that ijma' overrides the khabar because agreement of an era is infallible. If no ijma' is reached, the earlier statement remains valid for taqlid.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the qualified mujtahids of a particular era on a ruling.
الخبر (al-khabar): An isolated report (khabar wahid) that is not mutawatir.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a shar'i ruling by a later revealed text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented, when can ijma' be validly concluded contrary to a khabar wahid?
A) When the khabar is definitively established and its ruling remains
B) When the khabar may be abrogated or weak
C) Never, because the khabar always constitutes a dissenting opinion
D) Only if the khabar is mutawatir

Key Takeaway
Ijma' can override a khabar wahid if the khabar is weak or possibly abrogated; but if it is definitively established and unabrogated, ijma' cannot contradict it.
